After I have completed for you, children, this book, which is the last of the science in medicine with its completion, and have reached its end in its expositions and its declarations, it has seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise, which is a part of operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since the operation with the hand has been laid low in our region and in our time utterly private—until perhaps its science has perished, and its trace has been cut off—and there remain from it only small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which have been altered by hands, and error and hesitation have befallen them, until its intentions have been closed, and its sight has been withdrawn—it has seemed to me to revive it with the ordering of this treatise in it, according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation, and to come with forms of cautery instruments and the other instruments of the work, with the addition of declaration and with the hastening of that which is necessary.
The cause however for which a good craftsman of it is not found with his hand in this our time is: that the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to be exercised beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galen narrated, until he knows the aids to the limbs, and their forms, and their connection and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their exits, and of the pulsating and still veins, and the places of their exits.
And because of that Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with a work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We however have already said about that in the introduction of this book.
Since he who is not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy is not deterred from falling into error, whereby people are killed, just as I have seen many of those who are formed in this science and boast about it without knowledge and without experience.
That is, because I saw a foolish physician cut an abscess in the neck of a woman, and cut some arteries in the neck, wherefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead between his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to extract a stone from a man who had advanced in age, and the stone was large. So he reached it and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been called to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone, and the disposition of the sick man, that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving a stipend from a certain Duke of our land for medicine: and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him, a fracture in his leg near the heel: and the physician, with his ignorance, hurried and bound the fracture over the wound with pillows and splints with strong constriction, and did not allow the wound any breathing space.
Then he dismissed him according to his own desires. Afterwards, he dismissed him after a few days, and instructed him not to loosen the bandage: and he stood like that until his leg and his foot were festered, and he arrived at death.
Therefore, I was called to him: and I hurried to loosen the bandage: and tranquility followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, the corruption had already become confirmed in the limb: and I was unable to restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to wander in the limb until he died.
And I saw another physician, who pierced the cancerous abscess: and it ulcerated after days, until its malice increased with its master.
That is because when the cancer is pure, from melancholic humor, then it is not necessary to reach it with iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate its being completely severed.
And therefore, children, it is necessary for you to know that surgery, with the hand, is divided into two divisions: namely, surgery to which health is joined; and surgery with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already roused in every place of this book, in which comes the surgery, in which is terror and fear.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of it, and to diminish it, so that fools may not find a way to speak ill of and dishonor it.
Therefore, take the measure with diligence and protection, and your sick with ease and firmness, and use the better path leading through God's grace to health and praiseworthy success; and leave the terrible illnesses of difficult cure; and remove your souls from that which causes you fear, so that hesitation may not enter into your faith and your advantage.
For there remains more for your glory, and higher things in this world, and finally for your possessions.
For Galen already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat a bad illness, lest you be called a bad physician.
However, I have now divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
Concerning the cautery with fire, and the cautery with sharp medicine, detailed and arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments, and the ironwork of the cautery, and everything that is necessary in the operation.
Second Chapter.
Concerning incision and perforation, phlebotomy and cupping, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things: and all detailed, arranged in the form of instruments.
Third Chapter.
Concerning restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting, and similar things: detailed, arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
But before I recall the operation with it, it is necessary for me to speak of the quality of its benefits and harms, and in what complexion it should be applied.
I say, therefore, that the discussion of the quality of the cautery's benefit and harm is a lengthy and subtle discussion, a matter of knowledge and hidden secrets.
Many wise men have spoken on it, and disagreed; and for me, a little from their words is enough, fearing length.
I say, therefore, that cautery benefits every complexion, with or without matter, except for two complexions: a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
However, they disagreed about the hot and dry complexion with matter. For some said that cautery is helpful in it. And others said the opposite, namely that cautery is not suitable in an illness caused by heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat; and it is unsuitable that one be healed from a hot and dry illness by heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite stated that through cautery, help is given in every hot and dry illness that occurs in human bodies, because when you compare a human body and its humors to the complexion of fire, you find the human body to be cold.
And I indeed say through his statement: because experience has already shown me that on several occasions.
However, it is not appropriate for one to come upon it unless one has already been proven and trained in the final exercise of the cautery chapter, and has known the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of illnesses in themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and their duration of time.
From the other complexions, however, there is no fear for you; and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For now all physicians have agreed upon them, and have not disagreed in their use of cautery in them.
And know, children, that from the secret of healing through cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine, is that fire is simple, whose action does not reach except the member that is cauterized, and does not harm another member joined to it, except with small harm.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches that which is distanced from the members, and perhaps causes illness of difficult healing in a member, and perhaps kills it.
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do that unless it overflows.
Now, however, that has become known to us through experiment, because of the length of service and study with the art, and our station upon the truth of things; and for that reason I excuse myself from the length of the discourse.
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to this book of mine, I would present to you the hidden secret in fire, and the quality of its operation on bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses with a demonstrative philosophical discourse, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree on the time in which the cautery should be applied, and prefer the time of spring.
And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm that is incidental to the time is submerged in the benefit that is attracted by the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary, strong, urgent pains, which do not tolerate slowness; because it is feared that from them greater harm will result than the slight harm caused by delay.
And do not let it enter your minds, O children, that which only the common people and foolish physicians fear, namely, that the illness cured by cautery does not always return; and they consider that a consequence, and the matter is not as they suppose: because cautery is not unless in the place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries the humidities which are the cause why pains occur.
However, cautery surpasses medicine in the swiftness of its cure, and the power of its action, and the vehemence of its dominion; and it is possible for the illness to return at some time according to the patient's complexion, and the location of his illness, and its power; and what is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in it; and what comes to him in its acquisition from foods and similar causes, unless it be an illness in which cautery is administered.
A subtle illness in a limb from few superfluities and humidities, such as toothache, and similar to it, for pain; it is possible that that pain will not return in it. But that happens in few cases.
But truly the common people's assertion that cautery is the last resort of medicine is correct; not for what they intend by that, since they believe that there is no cure that compares with medicine, nor any after the cautery has passed.
However, the matter is the opposite of that, and the intention that cautery is the last resort of medicine is not, except that when we administer methods of treatment for some illness, and those medicines do not work; then we administer cautery at the end of things, and it works: then from there it falls, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention understood by the common people and many unskilled physicians.
However, the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron; and they did not say that except because of the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance; and they said that the place of the cautery does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely so; since I have already tested it, and found that it does not do that in some bodies without others.
And cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, just as they said. However, when you make a cautery of fire from gold, it is not clear to you when it is heated to the quantity you desire, because of the redness of the gold; and when it rapidly approaches the cold, and if you add more heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls from that occupation; and because of that, cautery with iron is quicker and more effective with us, by reason of its suitability for the operation.
And I indeed have already arranged this chapter on cautery, according to chapters; and I have arranged them from head to foot, so that they may alleviate the seeker of what they wish from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization is beneficial in controlling the excess of moisture and coldness in the brain; these two are causes of headaches, and of the flow of humors from the head to the eyes and ears, and of excessive sleep, and toothache, and sore throat; and universally, every sickness that arises from cold, such as paralysis, headaches, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is, that you should first prescribe to the sick person a cleansing, resolving medicine for the head for three or four nights, according to the strength of the sick person, and his age, and his habit.
Then command him to shave his head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands in a square posture, so that he has placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the root of your palm upon the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger arrives, mark that place with the cautery.
Then apply the olive-shaped cautery to the fire.
Then place him upon the place marked with the cautery, descending, so that your hand is gradually constrained, and you revolve him. Then quickly lift your hand, and observe the place.
If you see now exposed from the bone a quantity of alkali or a quantity of zeuherb, then raise your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the iron itself, or with another from it if it cools down: until the bones, which I told you, appear.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak in it cotton, and place it on the place, and leave it for three days.
Then place on top of the cotton soaked in butter, and leave it on the place, until the scab of fire is destroyed. Then treat it with the four-drug ointment, until it is healed.
They have said that the more a wound remains open, the more it emits pus: therefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should be held until something of the thickness of bone is burned.
Then scrape away that which has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that it is necessary to reach the ultimate with the cautery, until it makes an impression on the bone, so that the bone falls away, which is done like the shape of a kirate; or the instrument that women use in pouring small alphabetic ink.  And they believe that vapors from the head are driven out from this place, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then treat it until it is consolidated.
However, these two types of cautery do not seem to me to be at all appropriate except in some men according to the way of fear.
And to leave it [the wound] is, in my opinion, better with regard to his health.
For the head is weakened by the breaking of its natural continuity, as we have testified in the other members; and especially when the head of the weak person is naturally feeble.  And indeed the first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it; therefore operate with it in health.
Chapter 3.
When chronic pain occurs in the whole head, and it is prolonged in the sick person, and he uses leeches, and cupping, and head-purges, and oils, and emollients. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the one cautery that we have described, and if none of those [treatments] helps him, then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong natural constitution, and not weak, and it finds a vehement cold, then cauterize with another cautery slightly under the [previous] one. Then cauterize it above every horn of its head with a cautery, so that it does not pierce the skin, and a quantity of bone, as we have described, is uncovered. And cauterize it with a single cautery on the occiput of its head, in the place called *vas* (or vessel): and it is the place where a cupping is placed.  And elevate your cautery in this, and do not uncover bone. For the sick person finds, because of that, a vehement pain, and different from the pain of the other cauteries of all the head.
And I say that this cautery should be in its place: and it should be a cautery with which the horns of the head and its occiput are cauterized, a finer cautery than the one used for cauterizing the middle of the head.
Chapter IV.
When pain and throbbing occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is cleansed with purifying medicines, and the remaining treatment, which I described in the divisions of illnesses, is administered, and it does not benefit the whole: then cauterization is performed in it according to two methods: either cauterization with a burning, sharp medicine, or with iron.
The cauterium with a burning, sharp medicine is to take one clove of garlic, and peel it, and cut off its ends from both sides. Then dissect the painful area at the time with a broad phlebotom, until a space under the skin is made in which the clove is placed.
Then insert it into the space beneath the skin until it is hidden; then bind over it with a suitable constricting bandage, and leave it for a quantity of fifteen hours, then loosen it, and remove the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days. Afterward, apply to it a poultice soaked in butter until the area produces pus; then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, do it with certain burning medicines, which I wrote in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
The cauterization of it with iron, however, is according to this method. The cautery iron, whose form is this.
And it is called a nail, because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is something of a curve, and in its middle there is a small eminence.
Then place it upon the place, and hold your hand; and you shall turn the iron gradually with speed; and the quantity that is burned shall be from the thickness of the skin, like half of it. And raise your hand, so that the artery, which is below, is not burned, and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak a cloth in salt water, and place it on the area, and leave it for three days; then place a cloth with butter; afterward treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second cautery's knife-edge. And beware of cutting the artery in this hemicrania, not an old one properly.
Concerning the method of cauterizing an old hemicrania.
When treating hemicrania, with what we have said from the preceding treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of diseases, and if the treatment does not help; and you see from the disease that what we have said about the first cautery with medicine, or with cautery with fire, is not sufficient, then it is necessary to heat the cautery knife until it turns white after you have marked the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or about that; and place your hand on one side, and press it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jaw, which moves during mastication, lest the side or nerve that moves it be burned, whence spasm may result.
And be on guard, and cautious of the flow of blood from the artery that has been cut. For in its cutting lies danger, and especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not diligent or skilled; and he abandons the operation with it at the outset.
And I will come with a reminder of the regimen for the blood flow occurring from the artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
If you see from the sickness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see the body of the sick person tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with the cautery having two knives. For this cauterization is better and more beneficial.
Concerning the method of cauterization in earache.
When earache occurs from cold, and is treated with remedies, and the rest of the treatment that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain is not removed, then apply a cautery: and it is that which is called the Point, whose form is this.
Then, after its ignition, points with it around the entire ear, as it revolves; or around each, if the pain is in both at the same time. And move the cautery slightly away from the root of the ear, after you have marked the places with ink: and let the quantity of cautery be ten points in each ear, and like that.
Then treat the places until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Torture.
Chapter VII.
Torture that is cured with cauterization is only from the types that arise from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterization of the type that arises from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this type of torture with leeches, and head-cleansings, and gargles, and your treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that you cauterize the afflicted with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and a second slightly lower on its temporal area, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the afflicted part. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with a cautery directly at the tip of the upper part of the ear, below the horn of the head, slightly; and another on the temporal region, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And hold your hand with the cautery until a quantity equal to half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type from the knife, whose form was previously mentioned; however, it is not much thinner than that, as you see; and it ought to be a knife with a little superfluous thickness.
Then treat the places with that which preceded, until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in ancient Apoplexy.
When the apoplexy is longstanding, and you have treated it with what we have said, and your treatment is of no benefit, and the sick person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries upon each horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said, and with a cautery in the back of the head, according to what preceded: and the method of the cautery should be according to what preceded.
Also, cauterize with a cautery on the opening of the stomach; and this is more of a last resort.
Then, treat him with what preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that large doses of hyerae and pills that cleanse the brain be given to the sick person first.
Then shave the sick person's whole head, and place on his occiput a plaster of synapis as described in the treatise on plasters; and apply it several times.
For this is the method of the cautery; and do it according to the same order as I have said there.
If, therefore, it heals by that, it is good. If not, then make three cauteries on the posterior part of his head, which shall descend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye; and place the thickness of a finger between each cautery.
Then treat the cautery, with what went before.
If however you wish an addition, and the sick person is tolerant of it, then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish an addition, then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then treat him until he is healed; and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the form which was given previously.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed in cleansing the head with hyssop, and with what we have said.
Then shave the head of the sick person; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery above each horn of the head, and with a cautery above its back, and with three above the vertebrae of the neck.
If, however, in the sickness there is a need for softening the body with more than those, and the sick person is tolerant, and the illness is severe: then cauterize him with four cauteries above the vertebrae of the back, and lastly with a cautery, until most of his skin is burned, and raise your hand. Then treat him until he is healed: and thus the cautery is Olive.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, unless that one whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you first cleanse his brain with leeches, and with the other treatment that we have described in the division, when the patient is strong, or is tolerant in taking medicines.
However, if it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and chewing motions that cleanse the brain are administered, many days beforehand with improvement in the diet.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the manner: and with another cautery on his occiput, and with a cautery over every horn of his head. If however, the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I mentioned in the case of paralysis, and for the softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the method which preceded.
If however the patient is a child, then apply a thin cautery, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that we mentioned in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of downward melancholic influence, and the patient's body is moist, then give him a drink that will cleanse his brain, according to what has been previously described in the division: then shave the patient's head, and afterwards make a neatly fashioned pad of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head, and the patient, seated upright, must be held in place on all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is better made from old sheep's butter. And heat it over a fire with a moderate amount of heat, such that a finger can tolerate it when placed inside. Then apply it to the center of his head in a circular motion, and let it remain until it cools.
Do this for the sick person once every week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures throughout it, so that you hold the cautery, indeed, while smelling it.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then place over it a poultice soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs, which I have stated in the division, then begin and let the weak drink it, with that which will cleanse his head.
And guard him from all moisture, and make him sit in a bath, in fasting for a few days.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him over both temples with two cauteries, if the descent of water is in both eyes simultaneously; or from one side, if the descent of water is in one eye; and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries which are under the skin; and let the cauteries be long in the width of the temples; and beware of the flow of blood.
If you see anything from it, then cut it away immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with the knowledge that is in the extraction of arteries, and the cutting of them, and caution against the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under the two bones, with two cauteries finally applied.
Concerning the method of cauterization in ancient lachrymal cases.
When the tears of the eyes are old, persistent, and are above the veins and arteries that are on the exterior head, it is ascertained that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then cauterize with the same cautery as I have described in the beginning of descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries over the two temples, and two cauteries on the neck under the two bones. And if it needs further application, then cauterize it on every side of the eye cautiously, above the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing for a foul smell from the nose.
When you treat it, with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then act quickly and give the weak decoctions in a drink for three nights; afterwards shave his head and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an olive cautery. Then cauterize it with a claw cautery, using two cauteries, above the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And guard against the artery, lest you strike it.
And this is the form of the Claw cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows slightly with two cauteries on every side: and they should be spaced apart by two times their width: and the length of each cautery should be according to the length of the eyebrow: and do not bring your hand with the cautery to the furthest point, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is burned.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs are inverted and prick the eye.
The cautery is of two types: either a cautery with fire, or a cautery with a burning medicine.
In the cautery with fire, first instruct the patient to remove his hairs, if he is one who trims them, until they are extended and equal. If, however, they prick him at their origin, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they grow out.
When they have grown out and are equal, then place the patient's head in your lap; then mark upon the eyelid of his eyes with ink, a mark in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a cotton swab soaked in egg white, or in psyllium mucilage, over the eye.
Then apply the cautery, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the shape that you marked, gradually in many stages, until the surface of the skin, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burned away.
And the sign of the success of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting, and the hairs rising near the puncture of the eye.
Therefore, lift your hand then, and leave it for three days.
Then place over it a poultice with butter, until the eschar is removed. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
If any of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid softens, then cauterize that place again, as you did at first.
If however the hairs are in the lower part, then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural position and made even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is that you command the infirm person to let the hairs grow until they are extended and even. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from paper on cloth.
Then take from known soap and from unleached lime each a weight of one ounce or nearly that: then rub them together with good trituration, and do it quickly, lest it become cold. Then take from the paste that you made from it over the paper that you made as the form of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one eye, or of two. And place under the eye a poultice soaked in egg white: and let the head of the infirm person be in your bosom.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it a little. And you shall move it whenever the infirm person feels the biting of the medicine: because its biting is found as fire.
While therefore that which he finds as biting persists, then leave the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid rise, as it rises upon contraction with fire, or with incision, it is well; and if not, then again place upon it of the medicine upon the place where the medicine does not imprint, and does not darken, until your operation is equalized, and the eye contracts.
Then place upon it Cotum with butter, until the skin of the burn is eradicated. Then treat it with diaphinicon ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you in the operation, that you guard the ultimate guard, lest anything of the medicine fall into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after days, and something fights out of the hairs into the eye, then again place medicine upon that place which softens from the eyelid properly, as you did at first. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that let your consideration be: and the path of righteousness is not hidden from him who has a study of this art.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a tear duct fistula.
When you treat a fistula, in the same way as we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then you ought to cauterize it according to this method.
Tell the sick person to place their head in your lap, and let the attendant hold their head between their hands in such a way that it does not move or shake with their head.
Then place a cautery, steeped in egg white or in psyllium mucilage, on their eye.  Then, apply the cautery, the shape of which is like this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's wing feather from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you wish it to penetrate right to the other end, and if you wish it to be held so upwardly.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and draw out the pus from it, and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it, and draw out its pus.
Then place the cautery, made very hot, upon it.
And hold your hand with the cautery near the eye, toward the nose, so that your hand does not wander or the sick person be disturbed; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If therefore you reach the beginning of your cautery up to the bone, it will be well. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it; and leave it for three days.
Then place a bandage with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it is healed.
If forty days have passed and it is not healed, then place a sharp corrosive medicine on it, until the bone is exposed; and scrape it according to what is in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing fistulas, which some of the first [practitioners] said. Attend to the location of the fistula, and split it; then place in the fissure a fine camahan, that is, a fine cannula, whose form is this. And pour into it a drachm of melted lead, and hold your hand with the cannula firmly, and let the sick person not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run or reach his eye.
And it is necessary that you place over the sick person's eye a poultice soaked in egg white, or in water.
For lead burns the area of the fistula and heals it with a remarkable cure.
If the fistula is healed by what we have said of cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nasal passage, and to reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to where it will come to its proper place.
Concerning the method of cauterization in lip fissures.
Often fissures occur in the lip, which are called hairs, and especially in the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, as we have said in the division of diseases, and treatment is not effective, then use a small knife cautery with fire, according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the sharpness of the knife.
Then place it, heated, quickly onto the fissures themselves, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a cautery, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth; then it forms pus and bursts; afterward it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and a fistula forms; then you treat it, and treatment does not help it, then it is necessary to cauterize the fistula with a cautery according to its size. Then insert the heated cautery into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches its depth and end, do this once or twice.
Then treat it afterwards with what we have said about treatment until it is healed.
If therefore the pus is cut off and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place and remove the corrupted bone according to what is in its head.
Concerning the method of cauterization in softened gums and teeth.
When the gum softens because of moisture, and the teeth move, and you treat it with remedies, and it does not help: then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then, with fire, a cautery, whose shape will come after these things, so that you place the cannula on the tooth: and quickly insert the heated cautery into it: and hold your hand for a short time, until the sick person feels the heat of the fire having already reached the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand; then repeat the cautery several times, according to your will.
Then let the sick person fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour: and let him spit it out.
For the moved tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupt moisture is dried.
On the method of cauterizing in toothache.
When toothache is due to coldness, or there is cold or worm within, and treatment with medicines does not help: then a cautery should be applied to it in two ways: either a cautery with butter, or a cautery with fire.
Its cautery with butter is that you should take fresh butter and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a vessel. Then take a wick, and wrap it around the end of the probe. Then immerse it in the boiled butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools; then repeat it several times, until the power of fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or a wick in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place heated iron upon it until fire reaches the depth of the tooth's cavity.
Its cauterization with fire is to hold a bronze or iron cannula. And let there be something of its thickness, so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the infirm person's bone.
Then, take a cautery whose shape will come, and place it upon that tooth, and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do it several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or on another.
And it is necessary, in the impression of that cautery, that the sick person fill his mouth with good butter, and hold it for one hour, then spit it out.
And this is the shape of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever extremity you are able, and this is the shape of the Cannula.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Strophuls.
When strophuls are caused by phlegm and cold humors, and are not amenable to digestion by medicines, and their digestion is required swiftly, then use a concave cautery, whose shape is this.
Having two open extremities, so that smoke may escape from the cautery through the other extremity; and place it, ignited, upon the abscess once, and a second time, if it needs it, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small, then place the cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a poultice infused in butter, until that which the fire burned is removed.
Then treat it with a tooth ointment, until the shape of the cannula is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humidities overcome the bronchial tube, and especially when it is with a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the weak person be evacuated first with loosening medicines.
Then cauterize it in the nocrati at the root of the throat in a depressed place; and beware, lest you reach with the cautery to the throat, nor to the skin, unless something of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck in the last vertebra of it, finishing it; and let the cautery be narrow according to the manner that preceded.
Then treat it with what preceded until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in diseases of the lungs and cough.
When cough and lung disease are from cold humors, and the sick person does not have a fever, nor consumption, and the illness is long-standing, then cauterize him with two cauteries above the fork in low, smooth, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be of a tube shape according to the form that preceded.
And if your desire is cauterization by puncturing with a cautery, which is called "Punctum," whose form preceded in the puncturing of ear pain: and let the punctures be from thirty punctures, up as though to others.
Then treat him with that which preceded, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, cauterization will be alleviated when you do it with three cauteries at one time.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated due to moisture, and does not fix itself at the time of its return from dislocation, until it is accustomed to returning, then it is dislocated by a small movement which happens as we have already testified, then you should reduce the dislocation first. Then the patient should be laid on their back, or on their healthy side. Then raise the skin that is in the inner Titillico upwards with the fingers of your left hand, and if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then take a cautery iron with two prongs. Whose form is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates it to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, why then the figure of the cauterization is of six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the fineness of the thread.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added to this manner, why there are eight cauteries.
Then place crushed leeks with salt upon the cautery. Then make the weak person adhere to tranquility, so that the limb does not move at any time, until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is upwards, and rarely does that happen, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a clavicle cautery, or with many cauteries by puncturing.
For the joint is strengthened, and moisture is removed: and the sick person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much moisture occur in the stomach, until they draw it out of its complexion, and phlegm multiplies upon it, and assiduous methods of treatment do not help: then it is necessary that the sick person be laid on his back, and extend his legs and hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, one cautery beneath the spoon of the chest the size of one finger with a clauili cautery, and two cauteries below on either side of a single cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And lengthen between each so they do not join, when they will make pus.
And the depth of the cautery be the amount of two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery which makes this cautery be one according to the form of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking him who is terrified by this cautery: and it is, that you mark upon the stomach a point according to the quantity, which you wish with encaustic: then cauterize it with a cautery of the point: then care for it with the treatment which preceded until it is healed.
Of the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When pain occurs in the liver from coldness and moisture, or from thick wind, until it departs from its natural complexion by an excess discharge, and the sick person is treated with what we have said, and it does not benefit him: then it is necessary that the sick person be placed on his neck, and mark with encaustic three cauteries according to this figure, and this same quantity over the lower liver below the hypochondria, where the man's elbow reaches: and let the space that is between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be according to the length of the body straight: and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity of that which is burned be, from the thickness of the skin, a quantity of half of it, not added: and let the sick person stand on his feet.
If however he is not standing, then let him be lying down, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you, indeed, to cauterize these cauteries with a knife cautery, when there is subtlety and prudence in your art.
And guard yourself so that you do not proceed too quickly in the cauterization, and the thickness of the entire skin is burned, for then the entire body is burned, and it reaches the intestines: because the skin there is thin, therefore know this.
Concerning the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When an exit occurs, and you wish to know if the abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the sick person is afflicted with pain, and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is intense sharpness with the pain; and you see already that the treatment has wearied its physicians.
Therefore, the sick person should lie on their back. Then mark the location of the abscess with ink; then apply a cautery that resembles a ray. And this is its form. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the entire skin is burned and reaches the siphac, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment for exits, until it is healed.
And it is not fitting for one to use this type of cautery unless their study in the medical art is prolonged, and through whose hands these illnesses have run their course with experience many times; then indeed may they dare to perform this sort of operation.
But truly, to abandon it is better for me.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Pleuritis.
The ancients said that cautery with aristolochia roots is for a cold pleurisy according to this method. And it is that you should take from dry, long aristolochia roots, one root longer than the rest, and it should be the thickness of a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and light it in fire. Then cauterize with one cautery at the junction of the fork with the neck, and with two small cauteries slightly sloping downward to the area under the beard.
And with two cauteries also at the area between the fifth and sixth ribs sloping slightly backward; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one at the area between the two shoulder blades; and with two cauteries from the two sides of the chest, below the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And you should not press your hand with the cautery, rather it should be visible, smelling the skin.
And some ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron similar to a rod; and they heat it and insert it into the area between the ribs until it reaches the abscess, and pus comes out; just as we said in the case of a liver abscess.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear that either the weak man dies immediately or a fistula occurs in the place, for which there is no cure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the spleen, Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, according to what we have said about treatment in the division of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then a cautery should be used in it in three ways, all of which are correct.
One of which is to make three or four cauteries, drawing lines along the length of the spleen, in the shape of the liver cauteries, whose figure preceded this.
And let there be between each cautery a distance equal to the thickness of a finger, or a little more or less.
And let the method of the cautery be the same as that which we described for the cautery of the liver.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; and let the sick person lie weak on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: to apply a cautery with two prongs, as we stated in the chapter on the dislocation of the humerus; and lift the skin, which is directly over the spleen, where the sick person's left elbow reaches; and let your lifting of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert two very hot prongs until you penetrate the skin on the other side with them; then withdraw the cautery; thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three prongs.
Then treat the cautery after you let it emit pus for many days; for it is more beneficial than all the previous treatments.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in dropsy.
The cautery does not fall upon dropsy unless properly applied.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment that we have described in the division, and the treatment does not work, then you should cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery above the stomach, and another cautery above the liver, and a cautery above the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach: and the depth of the cautery should be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, so that it emits pus for a long time.
And do not remove the sick person from treatment after the cautery with him; because it is necessary that two intentions be gathered in him: and healing will hasten to him with God's help.
The shape of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be nail-shaped, according to its previous form; and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its previous form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the feet and legs.
When abscesses develop in a hydrops patient, and they are filled with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize above the back of the foot, in the area between the auricular and annular bones.  Lift your hand with the cautery, and do not rotate it; then lift your hand, and do not repeat it at all.
For the yellow water will sweat out, and the cautery should be of this shape.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the blade end of the cautery; and let the cautery be made along the length of the leg, one below the knee and the other below that, approximately in the middle of the leg; and above each thigh, make two cauteries.  And leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water may sweat out from it; then treat it with the other things which we have said.
Concerning the method of cauterization in abdominal distension.
Chapter XXXV.
When abdominal distension is caused by cold and moisture, weakening the retentive and digestive powers of the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with methods of cure, but does not heal; and you see a weak patient tolerating a cautery of exuberant power, then cauterize him with a large cautery upon his stomach, according to what preceded in cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery, and with four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle nail-shaped cautery; and with a large cautery above the kidneys, or with two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moisture, and the patient tolerates it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the breastbone, and with a cautery on each hip; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.
For this is a beneficial treatment, whose help does not err.
Concerning the method of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they are from thick, cold humors, or corrupted moisture, and are treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries above the lower spine of the back under the almeidati a little triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel by about two fingers' breadth.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face becoming suppurated, then cauterize him above the stomach with a large cautery, according to what preceded: and with a cautery above his liver, and another on his spleen, with a clauili cautery: and leave the cautery open for a time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you excise althelul, then cauterize with a cautery that resembles a ray. Then introduce the burning cautery into the excised althelul: and with the last of your hand, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein through which blood flows: do this once, or twice.
If therefore the althelul are many, then cauterize each one with a cautery according to what we have described. Then treat them, with that which is beneficial to them from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery over the alcatin, it is more effective in helping.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter XXXVIII.
When the sick person does not respond to the incision and operation that we have described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he is cured with a cautery.
Therefore, when a fistula occurs in someone, and it becomes chronic, pus flows from it, and corrupted humors. Therefore, it is more fitting that you probe it with a thin probe. Then ascertain its depth with the probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is like a ray. Then insert yourself the ignited cautery into the fistula, and the quantity in which the cautery entered.
And repeat the cautery on it, until all those corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to your need.
And beware of burning the nerve, if there is one there, or a large vein; or if the fistula goes to the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then beware of all these places.
And do not do this, unless the fistula is in a fleshy place, and you think it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it is healed.
If however the place is sealed, and the matter is cut away from it, and it remains thus for a long time, then know that it is now completely healed.
And if matter is not cut away from it, then know that it is penetrating, or a corrupt opening is within it, or something like that from those, the remembrance of which will come in its place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the kidneys.
When pain in the kidneys occurs from cold or from a thick wind, and it lessens because of that of the sick person, then it is necessary to cauterize it above the almethen upon the kidneys themselves, with a cautery on every kidney with a cautery-clavil, the remembrance of which has preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time in the almeidate itself. Therefore, three lines will come. Therefore, the last will be more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening of the bladder occur due to cold and moisture, to the point where the sick person cannot retain urine, then cauterize it in the lower part of the summit above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic hair begin, and cauterize with one cautery from the right side of the summit and another from the left side of it; and let the length of this cauterization on each side be according to the width of a thumb's knot; and cauterize it with a cautery on the lower back, or with two cauteries, if that is necessary; and let this be according to the previous cautery's pattern.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and moisture occur in the womb, and it is prevented from conception, and her menses are corrupted, and their expulsion is delayed, and pain occurs to her upon their arrival, then it is necessary that she be cauterized with three cauteries in a circle around the navel, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery above, slightly below the back, or with two cauteries; and let the cautery be as before.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous humors discharge into the anus, and cause its expulsion from its place; and a sign of this is that one leg is prolonged over the other when compared together; and the place of the dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore, it is necessary that you cauterize the affected area above the anus itself with a similar circular cautery; after you mark it with ink in a circle around the anus as it revolves; and that the anus itself falls in the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not present for you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive cautery; and let the depth of the cauterization be according to the thickness of the entire skin.
Then treat it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and dampness; and the patient is treated with what we have stated in the division, and the treatment does not help, and it grows worse: then it is necessary to free the patient from thick humors with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar things. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cauterization in it is according to two ways: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is that you cauterize over the hip joint itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make them a good or bad depth. And let the space between each cautery be the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes, however, a cautery is made in the middle above the head of the hip itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the hip dislocation, one: so that the circle contains the whole hip.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery for Sciatica, when the pain adheres to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
However, if it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the thigh, over the place where the sufferer points there, where the pain is, and with your cautery on the shin four fingers to the wild side for a little while: and let the cautery be a knife-like one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
If the sufferer indicates that the pain extends to near the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a point cautery, three, or four, or more if it needs it.
And if he indicates the pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with one knife-like cautery.
And beware in all your cauterizations, lest you overdo it with the cautery so as to burn the nerve, or a large artery, and thus bring upon the sufferer ill harm, or contraction.
And truly I have already seen one and another, from those who have cauterized above the ankle and have overdone it in the cauterization, and the leg has swollen until the swelling reached the foot, and it was entirely perforated and the whole foot was corrupted: then there happened a loosening of the abdomen, and death afterwards.
If the pain is in two parts simultaneously, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain learned men said in the cauterization of the anca, of which this is the method of cautery. Make a similar cautery of iron, whose diameter be half a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date stone, or a little less: and within that cautery let there be a third cautery.
And let the space that is between every cautery be the quantity of a thumb's knot: and let the cauteries be open on both sides: and let their height be like a knot, or two knots: and make for them a handle of iron fitting well into the cauteries.
Then let it be heated in fire, until it turns red and throws off sparks: then let it be placed over the affected area of the anca, the sick person lying on their healthy side. Therefore cauterize it with three round cauteries at one time.
Then leave it for three days. Afterwards apply plasters with butter: and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasis says, with this kind of cautery, O children, we have used it little, because of the terror of its appearance, and because we have found few who will wait upon it.
However, it is a good cautery for him who endures it, and finds a place for it with him.
A cautery, however, is with burning medicines, so that you make two pieces of samian ware having a perforated armilla, into which descends a hinge of its gate, of bronze, or iron, the length of a wall: whose height should be two knots, or like themselves.
And let the space between both be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let that which contains them be joined together, according to this form.
Then place it upon a box of ashes, the sick person lying on their healthy side. And press your hand firmly upon the box of ashes. Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been warmed with fire for a short time, and hold it for the amount of an hour: and let the sick person tolerate its burning, and its cauterization, for he finds the burning like fire, until the burning ceases.
Then raise your hand with the instrument, and wipe the entire ash with sweet water; then leave it for three days.
And place butter upon it, until the blackness of the cauterization is removed; and leave it for a few days, and pus will run from it. For it is the last in healing.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a poultice on it containing water, in the same manner as you did for the ash.
And this is the method of warm water; and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, each one part: grind both, and put them in a new pot, whose bottom is pierced with a small hole, according to the amount that the radius will enter it: and place another glass pot beneath the bottom of the pot: and pour over the alkali and lime fresh water, so that both are submerged by a finger's breadth: after that, press them with your hand with a good pressure; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends to the lower part of the glass pot.
Then collect all that water, and pour it over other lime; and strain it until it is renewed.
For then it will be very strong and sharp, which is used in many surgical operations and in cauterizing other limbs. Because it produces the operation of fire itself.
And among medicines with which the anca is cauterized, also like tesisie, and honey of anacard, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen, indeed, narrating, recounted the cure of a certain man from ancient times, by which the pain of the anca and sciatic vein was cured; and he praised it as being very great. And he said, because he did not require any further treatment, and because he was healed in one instance, until he recounted that perhaps he entered a bath carried, and emerged from it already healed.
And it is to be taken from green seitaragi; and if green is not found, let dry, fresh, be taken; and it shall be ground much with a little fat, and placed upon the anca, where the pain is, or the leg, or in the thigh; and it shall be bound, and left for a quantity of three hours, or for the quantity that the infirm person feels sedation of the burning. Then immerse him in a bath.
When therefore his body becomes moist, immerse him in a chair. For the pain recedes, and he is healed.
And know that no one should use a cautery with these medicines, unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides, who also said that the dung of goats, when cauterized with it the sciatic vein, benefits it: and the cautery is performed in this manner. Take wool, and soak it in old oil, and place it upon the deep place that is between the big toe and the sole, and is closer to the sole.
Then take the dry dung of goats, and burn it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it upon the wool, and let it be, until it is extinguished. Then do it again. Therefore do not cease to do it, until the sensation above the mediation reaches the ankle, and the pain rests.
And this method of cautery is called cautery of the Vaccinum.
Concerning the cauterization of pain in the back.
Sometimes pain in the back occurs from many causes, either from an accident, or from a blow, or from the evacuation of superfluous matter, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and moist matter: and cautery indeed does not fall, except in this single type, which is made from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after the evacuation of the patient with foul pills, and similar things, they should be placed on the back, where the pain is, three lines according to the width of the almeidati itself, after marking with ink in each line five cauteries, or more according to the amount that comes from the tolerance of the patient's strength: and let cauterization be done with a cautery-point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries, with a medial clauile cautery, according to this form.
Concerning the method of cauterization in the beginning stages of a humpback.
This illness often occurs in young children.
And the sign of its beginning in children is: that a constriction occurs in their breathing upon elevation and movement; and you find at the last of the spinal vertebrae of the back and its nodules, that it has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see it, and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cauterium that is a circle of this shape.
And let the cauterium encompass the entire part of the vertebra equally; and if you wish to cauterize in a circle of the vertebra with a pointed cauterium, make two or three lines; and let the points be close together.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, lest you apply the cauterium to the hump which results from a spasm of the nerve.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in gout and pains of the joints.
When pains in the joints are from cold humours that flow to any part of the body, then when pains occur in the feet, it is the custom of physicians to call it gout properly.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of treatment, and the pains are not removed, then the cauterium removes them.
And it is that you cauterize it after evacuation around the joint of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to pierce on the surface of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees, or other joints, and that often happens, then cauterize it above each knee with three or four cauteries from every side, with this same claw-shaped cautery.
If however more of this cautery are necessary for you, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If however the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we have said about the cautery in its chapter.
If however the pains are only in the hands, then puncture the points in the circumference of the foci, as if two lines revolve.
If however pain remains in the fingers, then puncture them, above each knot, and above the ridge of the hand.
If however the pains ascend after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not remove the sick person from a good regimen, from the reception of medicines. For if a good regimen is made, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God with this cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the intestine, or the spermatic cord, descends towards the testicle, and it is in the beginning close by: then it is necessary that you command the sick person to give up eating on his own day. And let him use of the lenitives, so that the excrement descends from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands upon his back; and command him to hold his breath, until it emerges, or the spermatic cord, or the intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with ink under the rupture above the pubic bone, with a sign whose extremity is similar to half a circle towards the upper parts of the body.
Then with a cautery of this form, until it comes white and throws off sparks. Then reduce the intestine, or spermatic cord, to its concavity. Then let the assistant place his hand over the spot, so that the intestine does not come out; and you have now opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed a cushion beneath him, and another servant over his legs, and another over his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery upon that mark, with your hand holding the cautery upright. And hold it until you meet with its mouth; or again with it a second time, if you have not met with its mouth in the first.
And carefully observe for the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, so that you do not burn it, and that death or great harm befall the sick person through it.
And know that when you do not meet with the mouth with the cautery, your operation is of no use.
And the cautery should be small for children, according to their size.
Then treat with the remaining ointments until it is healed.
And let the sick person lie on their back for forty days until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary to give him nourishment for the duration of his treatment, to soften his stomach, so that his intestines do not protrude during straining and bowel movements.
Then when he wishes to rise after forty days, then apply a properly made bandage and let him keep it for another forty days.
And let him abstain from work, and from a full diet of food and drink, and from loud noises.
For when he follows this regimen, he is thus completely healed.
And I will describe the treatment of Ruptures with incision in his chapter.
When ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen, and are incipient, and there is a need to prevent them from worsening, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let the part that is cauterized be thus about a third of its size. Then treat him with what we said, and it will not worsen.
And some early authorities have said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this shape.
After it is marked with ink, and a line is placed that is across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line to the lower side. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery iron.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in pains due to a fall or blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When in some limbs pain from a fall or blow occurs, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of each limb be a cautery according to its size, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twist, and the pain from it.
If therefore it is healed from the first cautery, it is well. If not, then repeat the cautery upon it.
Because it is customary for these pains to shift from the limb to that which is near it. Therefore it is necessary to pursue them with cautery until the infirmity is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Leprosy.
Leprosy sufferers are sometimes greatly helped by cautery. And especially the kind of leprosy that arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore, consider the power to cauterize it itself.
If, therefore, the leprosy is persistent, and you have treated it with what we have said in the division, and it has neither subsided nor ceased; and you fear that the corruption may spread over his entire constitution: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the known head, and a second below it towards the forehead near the end of the hair, and two above the two horns, and one behind above the nape of the neck.
And keep your hand with the cautery for a little while, until it makes a small impression on the mouth, and the bark peels away from it: so that the exhalation of gross vapors from it may be alleviated, and cauterize also the spleen with the cautery, as has been previously mentioned.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the afflicted person, and is clearly visible: then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries on the two jaws, and with two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and with six on the vertebrae of the back, and with one large one on the alhasos near the base of the tail and one above it, on the almeidati itself; and with two on the anchas: namely, one on every ancha, and with two on the knees: one on each knee, and with two on the shoulders, and with two on the elbows, and with two on the soft parts of his chest; and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of his fingers and feet; and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and the folds of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, lest you burn them.
And sometimes a cautery is used on the comb bone, and another on the stomach bone, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the more it is a help, and the more beneficial.
And know that the sick person does not experience pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because his body is already numb.
And it is necessary that there be cauteries of varying sizes, and small, according to the members and joints; according to what was previously mentioned in the types of instruments.
Then treat the cautery with herb flour and honey, and with the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a state of stupor.
When any limb is numb, and is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize the numb limb with cauteries, according to the merit of the limb's size, whether great or small.
And let your cautery enter the thickness of the skin a little. Then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes a cauterization is performed on something that is numb, which happens to the hand, and foot, in the vertebrae of the back near the exits of the nerves that move that limb, and the numbness is removed.
But let no one presume upon it, unless he is wise in the anatomy of the limbs, and the exit of the moving nerves of the body.
Chapter LI.
When Albaras is old and nothing from the arts of medicine helps it, then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a short time, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color is changed.
Then treat it with flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and arnogloss leaves, and pigeon's blood, and swallow's blood; of each take one part: mix all these together, and spread them on a cloth, and apply to the place, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Cancer.
When the Cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, just as it revolves.
However, the wise have said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
However, it does not seem to me: because I fear that it will ulcerate, and I have already seen this happen several times.
And it is better that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Adubelati.
When someone has an Adubelati, and it is delayed in maturation, either because of excess making it so, or because of the infirmity of age, when he is decrepit, having little blood, or because of the time and the need to hasten the maturation of the Adubelati, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by puncturing. Then leave it. For it will hasten with maturation.
If however you wish to perforate it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, whose form is this.
And place it in the middle of the Adubelati until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery be from that which follows the infirm, so that the course of pus may be relieved.
Then treat it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in a corrosive evil.
Chapter LIIII.
Corrosion is not anything other than a corruption that walks in a member, and it corrodes it; just as fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see a corrosive in a place that can tolerate a cautery with fire, then use many cauteries of fire, small and large clamps, according to what will be suitable for that place where the corrosive is.
Then cauterize it from every side until you eradicate the entire corruption, and nothing of it remains completely.
Then leave it for three days, and place powdered sulfur with oil over the cauterized places, until all eschars and all corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days healthy flesh is born, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then repeat the cautery on whatever remains of the corrupted places.
And it is sometimes cured by corrosive medicine. For it indeed rises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of more rapid help; and I have already said that its cauterization with corrosive medicine is in division; therefore receive it there when you need it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in corns and warts.
Chapter LV.
This ailment often occurs in the lower parts of the feet, and is a thick, filtered substance that hurts the foot.
And cautery in them is of two kinds: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for cautery with fire, a concave cautery like the wing of a vulture should be heated; it should be made of iron, the size of the whole corn on all sides, and with thin edges.
Then place it, heated, on the corn. Then rotate the hand with the cautery around the corn, until the cautery reaches the depth of the corn, and leave it for three days, until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply a plaster with crushed wild mallows and salt, and leave the plaster on it overnight. It will indeed be eradicated from its roots.
Then treat the area with a flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
If they are not cured and repeatedly occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet, then apply a cautery with hot water to them; and you should take a cannula of bronze, or iron, or of a vulture's feather, and place it on the corn, or blister.
